
============== high level task decomposition ================
[{'objective': 'Mathematically model the torus and sphere surfaces and identify conditions for their external tangency along a circle.'}, {'objective': 'Calculate the radius of the tangent circle when the torus rests on the outside of the sphere in the first configuration (radius r_i).'}, {'objective': 'Calculate the radius of the tangent circle when the torus rests on the outside of the sphere in the second configuration (radius r_o).'}, {'objective': 'Compute the difference r_i - r_o, simplify it to lowest terms as a fraction m/n, and find m + n.'}]
============== task analysis ================
1. Extract and Summarize Given Information:
- A torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle.
- The axis of revolution is at a distance 6 from the center of the circle, producing a standard torus shape (a "donut").
- A sphere S has radius 11.
- The torus T is placed externally tangent to the sphere S in two different configurations, each time touching S along a circle.
- In these two configurations, the radii of the tangent circles on the torus are r_i and r_o respectively.
- The problem involves the difference r_i - r_o, which can be expressed as a reduced fraction m/n.

2. Analyze Relationships Between Components:
- The torus is defined by two parameters: the radius of the revolving circle (3) and the distance from the axis of revolution to the circle's center (6).
- The sphere of radius 11 is fixed.
- The torus rests on the outside of the sphere in two distinct ways, each producing an external tangency along a circle.
- The tangency along a circle implies that the torus and sphere surfaces touch along a common circle, not just a point.
- The radii r_i and r_o correspond to the radii of these tangent circles on the torus surface in the two configurations.
- The difference r_i - r_o is a key quantity, suggesting the problem involves understanding how the torus can be positioned relative to the sphere to produce these tangent circles.

3. Identify the Field of Study:
- The problem lies primarily in geometry, specifically 3D geometry involving surfaces of revolution.
- Concepts involved include toroidal surfaces, spheres, external tangency, and circle radii on surfaces.
- Subfields include differential geometry (surface properties), and possibly analytic geometry (equations of surfaces).
- Such problems are common in mathematical competitions and geometric modeling.

4. Highlight Aspects Needing Clarification:
- The problem states "when T rests on the outside of S" twice, which may imply two distinct positions or orientations; the exact nature of these configurations is not explicitly described.
- The terms r_i and r_o are defined as radii of tangent circles but it is not specified on which part of the torus these circles lie (e.g., inner vs outer circle of the torus cross-section).
- The exact positioning or orientation of the torus relative to the sphere in each tangent configuration is not detailed.
- Potential challenges include determining the locus of tangent circles and computing their radii without explicit coordinate systems or equations provided.

async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_sc_instruction_0 = (
        "Sub-task 0: Derive and validate the geometric and algebraic representations of the torus and sphere, "
        "including parametric or implicit equations, and characterize the conditions for external tangency along a circle. "
        "Use the given parameters: torus circle radius 3, axis distance 6, sphere radius 11."
    )
    N_sc_0 = self.max_sc
    cot_sc_agents_0 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.5) for _ in range(N_sc_0)]
    possible_answers_0 = []
    possible_thinkings_0 = []
    subtask_desc_0 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_0",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_0,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(N_sc_0):
        thinking0, answer0 = await cot_sc_agents_0[i]([taskInfo], cot_sc_instruction_0, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_sc_agents_0[i].id}, deriving geometric representations, thinking: {thinking0.content}; answer: {answer0.content}")
        possible_answers_0.append(answer0)
        possible_thinkings_0.append(thinking0)
    final_decision_agent_0 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking0, answer0 = await final_decision_agent_0([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_0 + possible_answers_0, 
                                                    "Sub-task 0: Synthesize and choose the most consistent and correct geometric and algebraic representations and tangency conditions.", 
                                                    is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 0 output: thinking - {thinking0.content}; answer - {answer0.content}")
    subtask_desc_0['response'] = {"thinking": thinking0, "answer": answer0}
    logs.append(subtask_desc_0)
    print("Step 0: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    debate_instr_1 = (
        "Sub-task 1: Identify and verify the two distinct tangent circle configurations (with radii r_i and r_o) on the torus when it rests externally tangent to the sphere, "
        "using the representations from Stage 0 and geometric constraints. Given solutions to the problem from other agents, consider their opinions as additional advice. Please think carefully and provide an updated answer."
    )
    debate_agents_1 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Debate Agent", model=self.node_model, role=role, temperature=0.5) for role in self.debate_role]
    N_max_1 = self.max_round
    all_thinking_1 = [[] for _ in range(N_max_1)]
    all_answer_1 = [[] for _ in range(N_max_1)]
    subtask_desc_1 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_1",
        "instruction": debate_instr_1,
        "context": ["user query", thinking0, answer0],
        "agent_collaboration": "Debate"
    }
    for r in range(N_max_1):
        for i, agent in enumerate(debate_agents_1):
            if r == 0:
                thinking1, answer1 = await agent([taskInfo, thinking0, answer0], debate_instr_1, r, is_sub_task=True)
            else:
                input_infos_1 = [taskInfo, thinking0, answer0] + all_thinking_1[r-1] + all_answer_1[r-1]
                thinking1, answer1 = await agent(input_infos_1, debate_instr_1, r, is_sub_task=True)
            agents.append(f"Debate agent {agent.id}, round {r}, identifying tangent circle configurations, thinking: {thinking1.content}; answer: {answer1.content}")
            all_thinking_1[r].append(thinking1)
            all_answer_1[r].append(answer1)
    final_decision_agent_1 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking1, answer1 = await final_decision_agent_1([taskInfo, thinking0, answer0] + all_thinking_1[-1] + all_answer_1[-1], 
                                                    "Sub-task 1: Given all the above thinking and answers, reason over them carefully and provide a final answer.", 
                                                    is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 1 output: thinking - {thinking1.content}; answer - {answer1.content}")
    subtask_desc_1['response'] = {"thinking": thinking1, "answer": answer1}
    logs.append(subtask_desc_1)
    print("Step 1: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    reflect_inst_2 = "Given previous attempts and feedback, carefully consider where you could go wrong in your latest attempt. Using insights from previous attempts, try to solve the task better."
    cot_reflect_instruction_2 = (
        "Sub-task 2: Compute the difference r_i - r_o, simplify the fraction to lowest terms, and express it as m/n with m and n relatively prime positive integers. "
        + reflect_inst_2
    )
    cot_agent_2 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    critic_agent_2 = LLMAgentBase(["feedback", "correct"], "Critic Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    N_max_2 = self.max_round
    cot_inputs_2 = [taskInfo, thinking0, answer0, thinking1, answer1]
    subtask_desc_2 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_2",
        "instruction": cot_reflect_instruction_2,
        "context": ["user query", thinking0, answer0, thinking1, answer1],
        "agent_collaboration": "Reflexion"
    }
    thinking2, answer2 = await cot_agent_2(cot_inputs_2, cot_reflect_instruction_2, 0, is_sub_task=True)
    agents.append(f"Reflexion CoT agent {cot_agent_2.id}, computing difference r_i - r_o, thinking: {thinking2.content}; answer: {answer2.content}")
    for i in range(N_max_2):
        feedback, correct = await critic_agent_2([taskInfo, thinking2, answer2], 
                                                "Please review and provide the limitations of provided solutions. If you are absolutely sure it is correct, output exactly 'True' in 'correct'", 
                                                i, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"Critic agent {critic_agent_2.id}, providing feedback, thinking: {feedback.content}; answer: {correct.content}")
        if correct.content == "True":
            break
        cot_inputs_2.extend([thinking2, answer2, feedback])
        thinking2, answer2 = await cot_agent_2(cot_inputs_2, cot_reflect_instruction_2, i + 1, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"Reflexion CoT agent {cot_agent_2.id}, refining difference calculation, thinking: {thinking2.content}; answer: {answer2.content}")
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 2 output: thinking - {thinking2.content}; answer - {answer2.content}")
    subtask_desc_2['response'] = {"thinking": thinking2, "answer": answer2}
    logs.append(subtask_desc_2)
    print("Step 2: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    cot_sc_instruction_3 = (
        "Sub-task 3: Aggregate the simplified fraction components m and n from the previous subtask to find the sum m + n as the final answer."
    )
    N_sc_3 = self.max_sc
    cot_sc_agents_3 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.5) for _ in range(N_sc_3)]
    possible_answers_3 = []
    possible_thinkings_3 = []
    subtask_desc_3 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_3",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_3,
        "context": ["user query", thinking0, answer0, thinking2, answer2],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(N_sc_3):
        thinking3, answer3 = await cot_sc_agents_3[i]([taskInfo, thinking0, answer0, thinking2, answer2], cot_sc_instruction_3, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_sc_agents_3[i].id}, aggregating m and n, thinking: {thinking3.content}; answer: {answer3.content}")
        possible_answers_3.append(answer3)
        possible_thinkings_3.append(thinking3)
    final_decision_agent_3 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking3, answer3 = await final_decision_agent_3([taskInfo, thinking0, answer0, thinking2, answer2] + possible_thinkings_3 + possible_answers_3, 
                                                    "Sub-task 3: Synthesize and choose the most consistent and correct final answer m + n.", 
                                                    is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 3 output: thinking - {thinking3.content}; answer - {answer3.content}")
    subtask_desc_3['response'] = {"thinking": thinking3, "answer": answer3}
    logs.append(subtask_desc_3)
    print("Step 3: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    final_answer = await self.make_final_answer(thinking3, answer3, sub_tasks, agents)
    return final_answer, logs

The torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, where the axis is at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. This is a standard torus with major radius R = 6 (distance from axis to circle center) and minor radius r = 3 (radius of the revolving circle). The implicit equation of such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis is:\n\n((sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + z^2 = r^2)\n\nOr equivalently, in implicit form:\n\n(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + R^2 - r^2)^2 = 4 R^2 (x^2 + y^2)\n\nHere, R=6, r=3.\n\nThe sphere S has radius 11 and is centered at the origin for simplicity, so its implicit equation is:\n\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 11^2 = 121\n\nThe external tangency along a circle means the torus and sphere surfaces touch along a circle. To have tangency along a circle, the intersection must be a circle where the surfaces touch externally.\n\nGiven the torus parameters and sphere radius, the two different tangent configurations correspond to the torus positioned so that the sphere touches the torus along two distinct circles on the torus surface. These circles correspond to different values of the torus parameter that define the cross-sectional circle radius at the tangent points.\n\nThus, the geometric and algebraic representations are:\n- Torus: (x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 36 - 9)^2 = 4 * 36 * (x^2 + y^2)\n- Sphere: x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121\n\nThe condition for external tangency along a circle is that the two surfaces intersect in a circle where their normals are parallel (gradients proportional), and the intersection set is a circle rather than isolated points.\n\nThis characterization sets the stage for further analysis of the tangent circle radii.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent ADl1:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, with the axis at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. The implicit equation of such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis is:\n\n((sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + z^2 = r^2)\n\nOr equivalently, in implicit form:\n\n(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + R^2 - r^2)^2 = 4 R^2 (x^2 + y^2)\n\nHere, R=6, r=3.\n\nThe sphere S has radius 11 and is centered at the origin for simplicity, so its implicit equation is:\n\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 11^2 = 121\n\nThe external tangency along a circle means the torus and sphere surfaces touch along a circle. For two surfaces to be tangent along a circle, their distance functions must coincide along that circle, and their gradients must be proportional there. The locus of points where the torus and sphere intersect is given by solving their equations simultaneously. To have tangency along a circle, the intersection must be a circle where the surfaces touch externally.\n\nGiven the torus parameters and sphere radius, the two different tangent configurations correspond to the torus positioned so that the sphere touches the torus along two distinct circles on the torus surface. These circles correspond to different values of the torus parameter that define the cross-sectional circle radius at the tangent points.\n\nThus, the geometric and algebraic representations are:\n- Torus: (x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 36 - 9)^2 = 4 * 36 * (x^2 + y^2)\n- Sphere: x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121\n\nThe condition for external tangency along a circle is that the two surfaces intersect in a circle where their normals are parallel (gradients proportional), and the intersection set is a circle rather than isolated points.\n\nThis characterization sets the stage for further analysis of the tangent circle radii.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent ADl1:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, with the axis at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. The standard implicit equation for such a torus, centered at the origin with symmetry about the z-axis, is:\n\n(√(x² + y²) - 6)² + z² = 3².\n\nThis can be rewritten in implicit form as:\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 6² - 3²)² = 4 * 6² * (x² + y²),\n\nor\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 36 - 9)² = 144(x² + y²),\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144(x² + y²).\n\nThe sphere S of radius 11 centered at the origin has the implicit equation:\n\nx² + y² + z² = 11² = 121.\n\nFor external tangency along a circle, the torus and sphere surfaces must be tangent along a common circle. This implies that the distance between the surfaces is zero along that circle, and their gradients (normals) are parallel there. The circle of tangency lies on both surfaces, so points on it satisfy both equations simultaneously and the tangency condition (equal normals up to scale).\n\nThus, the problem reduces to finding the set of points satisfying both implicit equations and the tangency condition. This characterizes the external tangency along a circle for the given parameters.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent WMrK:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the same plane, where the center of the circle is 6 units from the axis. The standard parametric equations for such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis are:\n\nx(u,v) = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u\n y(u,v) = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u\n z(u,v) = 3 sin v\n\nwhere u, v ∈ [0, 2π). This describes the torus as a surface of revolution with major radius R = 6 and minor radius r = 3.\n\nThe implicit equation of the torus can be derived from the distance to the axis and the radius of the revolving circle. The torus satisfies:\n\n(√(x² + y²) - 6)² + z² = 3²\n\nSquaring and rearranging, the implicit form is:\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 36 - 9)² = 4 * 36 * (x² + y²)\n\nor\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144 (x² + y²)\n\nThe sphere S with radius 11 centered at the origin has the implicit equation:\n\nx² + y² + z² = 11² = 121\n\nFor external tangency along a circle, the torus and the sphere must intersect in a circle where their surfaces touch externally. This means the distance between the surfaces is zero along a circle, and their normals coincide at every point on that circle.\n\nGeometrically, the intersection of the sphere and torus surfaces is a curve, and for tangency, this intersection is a circle where the surfaces are tangent. This imposes conditions on the gradients (normals) of their implicit functions being proportional on that circle.\n\nThus, the representation and tangency conditions are:\n\n- Torus implicit equation: (x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144 (x² + y²)\n- Sphere implicit equation: x² + y² + z² = 121\n- Tangency circle defined by the simultaneous solution of these equations with additional normal vector proportionality condition.\n\nThis sets the geometric and algebraic framework for characterizing the external tangency along a circle between the torus and sphere with the given parameters.\n\n### answer by Chain-of-Thought Agent ScCF:\nThe torus T with major radius R=6 and minor radius r=3 is represented by the implicit equation (x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 36 - 9)^2 = 4 * 36 * (x^2 + y^2), and the sphere S of radius 11 is represented by x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121. External tangency along a circle occurs where these two surfaces intersect in a circle, with their gradients proportional at every point on this circle, ensuring tangency rather than mere intersection.\n\n### answer by Chain-of-Thought Agent ADl1:\nThe torus T is given implicitly by (x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144(x² + y²), representing a torus generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis 6 units away. The sphere S is given by x² + y² + z² = 121. External tangency along a circle occurs where points satisfy both equations simultaneously and where the gradients of the two surfaces are parallel, indicating tangency along a circle.\n\n### answer by Chain-of-Thought Agent WMrK:\nThe torus T can be represented parametrically as x = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u, y = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u, z = 3 sin v with u,v in [0,2π), and implicitly by (x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144 (x² + y²). Use the given parameters: torus circle radius 3, axis distance 6, sphere radius 11. \n\n ### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent ScCF:\nTo derive the geometric and algebraic representations of the torus and sphere, we start with the given parameters. The torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, where the axis is at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. This is a standard torus with major radius R = 6 (distance from axis to circle center) and minor radius r = 3 (radius of the revolving circle). The implicit equation of such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis is:\n\n((sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + z^2 = r^2)\n\nOr equivalently, in implicit form:\n\n(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + R^2 - r^2)^2 = 4 R^2 (x^2 + y^2)\n\nHere, R=6, r=3.\n\nThe sphere S has radius 11 and is centered at the origin for simplicity, so its implicit equation is:\n\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 11^2 = 121\n\nThe external tangency along a circle means the torus and sphere surfaces touch along a circle. For two surfaces to be tangent along a circle, their distance functions must coincide along that circle, and their gradients must be proportional there. The locus of points where the torus and sphere intersect is given by solving their equations simultaneously. To have tangency along a circle, the intersection must be a circle where the surfaces touch externally.\n\nGiven the torus parameters and sphere radius, the two different tangent configurations correspond to the torus positioned so that the sphere touches the torus along two distinct circles on the torus surface. These circles correspond to different values of the torus parameter that define the cross-sectional circle radius at the tangent points.\n\nThus, the geometric and algebraic representations are:\n- Torus: (x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 36 - 9)^2 = 4 * 36 * (x^2 + y^2)\n- Sphere: x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121\n\nThe condition for external tangency along a circle is that the two surfaces intersect in a circle where their normals are parallel (gradients proportional), and the intersection set is a circle rather than isolated points.\n\nThis characterization sets the stage for further analysis of the tangent circle radii.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent ADl1:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, with the axis at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. The standard implicit equation for such a torus, centered at the origin with symmetry about the z-axis, is:\n\n(√(x² + y²) - 6)² + z² = 3².\n\nThis can be rewritten in implicit form as:\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 6² - 3²)² = 4 * 6² * (x² + y²),\n\nor\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 36 - 9)² = 144(x² + y²),\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144(x² + y²).\n\nThe sphere S of radius 11 centered at the origin has the implicit equation:\n\nx² + y² + z² = 11² = 121.\n\nFor external tangency along a circle, the torus and sphere surfaces must be tangent along a common circle. This implies that the distance between the surfaces is zero along that circle, and their gradients (normals) are parallel there. The circle of tangency lies on both surfaces, so points on it satisfy both equations simultaneously and the tangency condition (equal normals up to scale).\n\nThus, the problem reduces to finding the set of points satisfying both implicit equations and the tangency condition. This characterizes the external tangency along a circle for the given parameters.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent WMrK:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the same plane, where the center of the circle is 6 units from the axis. The standard parametric equations for such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis are:\n\nx(u,v) = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u\n y(u,v) = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u\n z(u,v) = 3 sin v\n\nwhere u, v ∈ [0, 2π). This describes the torus as a surface of revolution with major radius R = 6 and minor radius r = 3.\n\nThe implicit equation of the torus can be derived from the distance to the axis and the radius of the revolving circle. The torus satisfies:\n\n(√(x² + y²) - 6)² + z² = 3²\n\nSquaring and rearranging, the implicit form is:\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 36 - 9)² = 4 * 36 * (x² + y²)\n\nor\n\n(x² + y² + z² + 27)² = 144 (x² + y²)\n\nThe sphere S with radius 11 centered at the origin has the implicit equation:\n\nx² + y² + z² = 11² = 121\n\nFor external tangency along a circle, the torus and the sphere must intersect in a circle where their surfaces touch externally. The torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, where the axis is at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. This is a standard torus with major radius R = 6 (distance from axis to circle center) and minor radius r = 3 (radius of the revolving circle). The implicit equation of such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis is:\n\n((sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + z^2 = r^2)\n\nOr equivalently, in implicit form:\n\n(x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + R^2 - r^2)^2 = 4 R^2 (x^2 + y^2)\n\nHere, R=6, r=3.\n\nThe sphere S has radius 11 and is centered at the origin for simplicity, so its implicit equation is:\n\nx^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 11^2 = 121\n\nThe external tangency along a circle means the torus and sphere surfaces touch along a circle. For two surfaces to be tangent along a circle, their distance functions must coincide along that circle, and their gradients must be proportional there. The locus of points where the torus and sphere intersect is given by solving their equations simultaneously. To have tangency along a circle, the intersection must be a circle where the surfaces touch externally.\n\nGiven the torus parameters and sphere radius, the two different tangent configurations correspond to the torus positioned so that the sphere touches the torus along two distinct circles on the torus surface. These circles correspond to different values of the torus parameter that define the cross-sectional circle radius at the tangent points.\n\nThus, the geometric and algebraic representations are:\n- Torus: (x^2 + y^2 + z^2 + 36 - 9)^2 = 4 * 36 * (x^2 + y^2)\n- Sphere: x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121\n\nThe condition for external tangency along a circle is that the two surfaces intersect in a circle where their normals are parallel (gradients proportional), and the intersection set is a circle rather than isolated points.\n\nThis characterization sets the stage for further analysis of the tangent circle radii.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent ADl1:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the plane of the circle, with the axis at a distance 6 from the center of the circle. This implies that the distance between the surfaces is zero along that circle, and their gradients (normals) are parallel there. The circle of tangency lies on both surfaces, so points on it satisfy both equations simultaneously and the tangency condition (equal normals up to scale).\n\nThus, the problem reduces to finding the set of points satisfying both implicit equations and the tangency condition. This characterizes the external tangency along a circle for the given parameters.\n\n### thinking by Chain-of-Thought Agent WMrK:\nThe torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around an axis in the same plane, where the center of the circle is 6 units from the axis. The standard parametric equations for such a torus centered at the origin with the axis of revolution along the z-axis are:\n\nx(u,v) = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u\n y(u,v) = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u\n z(u,v) = 3 sin v\n\nwhere u, v ∈ [0, 2π). This describes the torus as a surface of revolution with major radius R = 6 and minor radius r = 3.\n\nThe implicit equation of the torus can be derived from the distance to the axis and the radius of the revolving circle. async def forward(self, taskInfo):
    from collections import Counter
    print("Task Requirement: ", taskInfo)
    sub_tasks = []
    agents = []
    logs = []

    cot_sc_instruction_0 = (
        "Sub-task 0: Define and derive the implicit and parametric equations of the torus and sphere, "
        "explicitly introducing a vertical displacement parameter h representing the offset of the torus tube center from the sphere center. "
        "Formulate the torus equation in shifted coordinates to correctly model the torus position relative to the sphere."
    )
    cot_sc_agents_0 = [LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Chain-of-Thought Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.5) for _ in range(self.max_sc)]
    possible_answers_0 = []
    possible_thinkings_0 = []
    subtask_desc0 = {
        "subtask_id": "subtask_0",
        "instruction": cot_sc_instruction_0,
        "context": ["user query"],
        "agent_collaboration": "SC_CoT"
    }
    for i in range(self.max_sc):
        thinking0, answer0 = await cot_sc_agents_0[i]([taskInfo], cot_sc_instruction_0, is_sub_task=True)
        agents.append(f"CoT-SC agent {cot_sc_agents_0[i].id}, define torus and sphere equations with displacement h, thinking: {thinking0.content}; answer: {answer0.content}")
        possible_answers_0.append(answer0)
        possible_thinkings_0.append(thinking0)
    final_decision_agent_0 = LLMAgentBase(["thinking", "answer"], "Final Decision Agent", model=self.node_model, temperature=0.0)
    thinking0, answer0 = await final_decision_agent_0([taskInfo] + possible_thinkings_0 + possible_answers_0, "Sub-task 0: Synthesize and finalize the torus and sphere equations with displacement h.", is_sub_task=True)
    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 0 output: thinking - {thinking0.content}; answer - {answer0.content}")

    logs.append(subtask_desc0)

    )

        "Present the final result clearly, referencing all prior verified derivations and simplifications."

    sub_tasks.append(f"Sub-task 3 output: thinking - {thinking3.content}; answer - {answer3.content}")
    subtask_desc3['response'] = {"thinking": thinking3, "answer": answer3}
    logs.append(subtask_desc3)
    print("Step 3: ", sub_tasks[-1])

    return final_answer, logs

The torus implicit equation is ((sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 = r^2). For external tangency along a circle, the surfaces must intersect along a circle and their normals must be parallel at points on this circle. Substituting the torus parametric form into the sphere equation yields (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121. The normal vectors are gradients of the implicit functions: sphere gradient ∇S = 2(x, y, z), torus gradient ∇F = (2(ρ - R)(x/ρ), 2(ρ - R)(y/ρ), 2(z - h)) with ρ = sqrt(x^2 + y^2) = R + r cos v. For parallelism, ∇F = λ ∇S for some scalar λ. Equating components leads to the relation h = R tan v. Thus, the external tangency conditions are the system: (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121 and h = R tan v, with R=6, r=3, and h,v variables. The torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius 3 around the z-axis, with the circle center at distance 6 from the axis. To model the torus position relative to the sphere, we introduce a vertical displacement parameter h, shifting the torus along the z-axis. The standard implicit equation of the torus centered at the origin is (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - 6)^2 + z^2 = 9. Replacing z by (z - h) to incorporate the vertical shift gives (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - 6)^2 + (z - h)^2 = 9. The parametric equations of the torus with parameters u, v in [0, 2π) are x = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u, y = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u, z = h + 3 sin v. The sphere remains centered at the origin with radius 11, implicit equation x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121. This formulation correctly models the torus and sphere with the vertical displacement h.\n\n### answer by Final Decision Agent FAlE:\nSphere S: Implicit equation x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121. Torus T: Implicit equation (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - 6)^2 + (z - h)^2 = 9, where h is the vertical displacement parameter. The parameters u and v correspond to the angles around the axis of revolution and around the minor circle, respectively. The parametric equations of the torus surface are x = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u, y = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u, z = h + 3 sin v, where h is the vertical displacement along the z-axis. The radius of the tangent circles on the torus at a given v is the distance from the axis of revolution to the point on the minor circle, which is r(v) = 6 + 3 cos v. This expression explicitly shows how the radius of the tangent circle varies with the parameter v on the torus surface, preparing for tangency analysis.\n\n### answer by Final Decision Agent 2fXQ:\nThe torus surface is parametrized by (u,v) as x = (6 + 3 cos v) cos u, y = (6 + 3 cos v) sin u, z = h + 3 sin v, with u,v in [0, 2π). The radius of tangent circles on the torus as a function of v is r(v) = 6 + 3 cos v.\n\n### Sub-task 1b: Derive the external tangency conditions between the torus and sphere, including the simultaneous solution of the shifted torus equation, the sphere equation, and the condition that their normal vectors are parallel at the tangent circle. Formulate these conditions as explicit algebraic equations involving h, R, r, sphere radius, and parameters u,v. Given solutions to the problem from other agents, consider their opinions as additional advice. Please think carefully and provide an updated answer. \n\n ### thinking #1 by Debate Agent QLyl:\nWe start with the sphere S centered at the origin with radius 11, described by the implicit equation x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121. The torus T is generated by revolving a circle of radius r = 3 around the z-axis at a distance R = 6, with vertical displacement h. The torus parametric form is x = (R + r cos v) cos u, y = (R + r cos v) sin u, z = h + r sin v, where u,v in [0, 2π). The torus implicit equation is ((sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 = r^2). For external tangency along a circle, the torus and sphere surfaces must coincide at points on that circle and their normals must be parallel (colinear). The tangent circle corresponds to fixing v and letting u vary from 0 to 2π, so the circle lies at constant v. We impose the two surface equations simultaneously: sphere: x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121, torus: (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 = r^2. Substituting the parametric torus coordinates into the sphere equation yields (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121. This is the first key equation relating h and v. Next, for normal vectors to be parallel at the tangent circle, the gradients of the implicit functions must be parallel. The gradient of the sphere is ∇S = 2(x, y, z). The gradient of the torus implicit function F is ∇F = (∂F/∂x, ∂F/∂y, ∂F/∂z). Expressing F as F = (√(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 - r^2, we compute partial derivatives: ∂F/∂x = 2(ρ - R)(x/ρ), ∂F/∂y = 2(ρ - R)(y/ρ), ∂F/∂z = 2(z - h), where ρ = sqrt(x^2 + y^2). At the point on the tangent circle: x = (R + r cos v) cos u, y = (R + r cos v) sin u, z = h + r sin v, and ρ = R + r cos v. So, ∇F = (2(ρ - R)(x/ρ), 2(ρ - R)(y/ρ), 2(z - h)) = (2 r cos v (x/ρ), 2 r cos v (y/ρ), 2 r sin v). The sphere gradient is ∇S = 2(x, y, z). For parallelism, ∇F = λ ∇S for some scalar λ. Comparing components, for x and y: 2 r cos v (x/ρ) = λ 2 x → r cos v / ρ = λ. For z: 2 r sin v = λ 2 z → r sin v = λ z. Using λ from x,y components: λ = r cos v / ρ, so r sin v = (r cos v / ρ) z → z = ρ tan v. But z = h + r sin v and ρ = R + r cos v, so h + r sin v = (R + r cos v) tan v. Rearranging gives h = (R + r cos v) tan v - r sin v. This is the second key equation relating h and v. The two equations to solve for h and v are: (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121, and h = (R + r cos v) tan v - r sin v. These equations define the external tangency conditions for the torus and sphere along a tangent circle parameterized by v and displacement h. The parameter u is free to vary along the tangent circle. This system can be solved to find the possible h values and corresponding v that yield tangent circles, and then the radii r_i and r_o = R + r cos v can be computed. Thus, the explicit algebraic system is: (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121, h = (R + r cos v) tan v - r sin v, with known constants R=6, r=3, sphere radius 11, and variables h, v. This formulation incorporates the shifted torus, sphere equation, and normal parallelism condition, completing the derivation of external tangency conditions.\n\n### thinking #1 by Debate Agent wWhM:\nWe start with the known implicit equations: the sphere S centered at the origin with radius 11, given by x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121, and the torus T with major radius R = 6 and minor radius r = 3, shifted vertically by h, with implicit equation (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 = r^2. The parametric form of the torus is x = (R + r cos v) cos u, y = (R + r cos v) sin u, z = h + r sin v, with u,v in [0, 2π).\n\nFor external tangency along a circle, the sphere and torus surfaces must intersect along a circle and their normal vectors at points on this circle must be parallel (collinear). This ensures a common tangent circle.\n\n1. Point on both surfaces: The point (x,y,z) lies on both surfaces, so it satisfies both implicit equations:\n   Sphere: x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121\n   Torus: (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 = r^2\n\n2. Using the parametric form of the torus, substitute x,y,z:\n   x = (R + r cos v) cos u\n   y = (R + r cos v) sin u\n   z = h + r sin v\n\n3. Sphere equation becomes:\n   ((R + r cos v) cos u)^2 + ((R + r cos v) sin u)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121\n   Simplifies to:\n   (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121\n\n4. The normal vector to the sphere at (x,y,z) is:\n   N_sphere = (2x, 2y, 2z) = 2(x,y,z)\n\n5. The normal vector to the torus at (u,v) can be found by gradient of its implicit equation or via parametric derivatives. For the torus implicit function:\n   F(x,y,z) = (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 - r^2 = 0\n\n   Gradient:\n   ∇F = (2(sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R) * (x / sqrt(x^2 + y^2)),\n          2(sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R) * (y / sqrt(x^2 + y^2)),\n          2(z - h))\n\n6. For the normal vectors to be parallel, there exists λ such that:\n   ∇F = λ * N_sphere\n\n   Componentwise:\n   2(sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R) * (x / sqrt(x^2 + y^2)) = λ * 2x\n   2(sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R) * (y / sqrt(x^2 + y^2)) = λ * 2y\n   2(z - h) = λ * 2z\n\n7. From the first two equations, if x,y ≠ 0, dividing both sides by 2x and 2y respectively, we get:\n   (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R) / sqrt(x^2 + y^2) = λ\n\n   Both yield the same λ, so the condition holds.\n\n8. From the third equation:\n   (z - h) = λ z\n\n9. Using λ from the first two equations:\n   λ = (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R) / sqrt(x^2 + y^2) = ( (R + r cos v) - R ) / (R + r cos v) = (r cos v) / (R + r cos v)\n\n10. Substitute λ into the third equation:\n    (z - h) = λ z\n    (h + r sin v - h) = λ (h + r sin v)\n    r sin v = λ (h + r sin v)\n\n11. Rearranged:\n    r sin v = (r cos v) / (R + r cos v) * (h + r sin v)\n\n12. Multiply both sides by (R + r cos v):\n    r sin v (R + r cos v) = r cos v (h + r sin v)\n\n13. Expand:\n    r R sin v + r^2 sin v cos v = r h cos v + r^2 cos v sin v\n\n14. Notice r^2 sin v cos v terms on both sides cancel out:\n    r R sin v = r h cos v\n\n15. Divide both sides by r (r ≠ 0):\n    R sin v = h cos v\n\n16. Therefore, the tangency condition relating h, R, and v is:\n    h = R tan v\n\n17. Recall from step 3 the sphere equation in terms of v and h:\n    (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121\n\n18. Substitute h = R tan v into this:\n    (R + r cos v)^2 + (R tan v + r sin v)^2 = 121\n\nThis is the key algebraic equation relating R, r, h, and v for external tangency along a circle where the normal vectors are parallel.\n\nSummary of conditions:\n- Sphere equation at tangent circle:\n  (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = sphere_radius^2 (here 121)\n- Normal vector parallelism:\n  h = R tan v\n\nThese two equations must be solved simultaneously for h and v to find the tangent circle parameters. Parameter u is free (0 to 2π) since the circle is generated by revolving around the z-axis.\n\nHence, the external tangency conditions are:\n\n(1) (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = sphere_radius^2\n(2) h = R tan v\n\nwith parameters R=6, r=3, sphere_radius=11, and variables h,v. Parameter u is arbitrary on [0,2π). This fully characterizes the external tangency configurations with tangent circles on the torus and sphere surfaces.\n\n### thinking #1 by Debate Agent mUtv:\nTo derive the external tangency conditions between the torus and the sphere, we start with the given equations and parameters. Next, for normal vectors to be parallel at the tangent circle, the gradients of the implicit functions must be parallel. The gradient of the sphere is ∇S = 2(x, y, z). The gradient of the torus implicit function F is ∇F = (∂F/∂x, ∂F/∂y, ∂F/∂z). Expressing F as F = (√(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 - r^2, we compute partial derivatives: ∂F/∂x = 2(ρ - R)(x/ρ), ∂F/∂y = 2(ρ - R)(y/ρ), ∂F/∂z = 2(z - h), where ρ = sqrt(x^2 + y^2). At the point on the tangent circle: x = (R + r cos v) cos u, y = (R + r cos v) sin u, z = h + r sin v, and ρ = R + r cos v. So, ∇F = (2(ρ - R)(x/ρ), 2(ρ - R)(y/ρ), 2(z - h)) = (2 r cos v (x/ρ), 2 r cos v (y/ρ), 2 r sin v). The sphere gradient is ∇S = 2(x, y, z). For parallelism, ∇F = λ ∇S for some scalar λ. Comparing components, for x and y: 2 r cos v (x/ρ) = λ 2 x → r cos v / ρ = λ. For z: 2 r sin v = λ 2 z → r sin v = λ z. Using λ from x,y components: λ = r cos v / ρ, so r sin v = (r cos v / ρ) z → z = ρ tan v. But z = h + r sin v and ρ = R + r cos v, so h + r sin v = (R + r cos v) tan v. Rearranging gives h = (R + r cos v) tan v - r sin v. This is the second key equation relating h and v. The two equations to solve for h and v are: (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121, and h = (R + r cos v) tan v - r sin v. These equations define the external tangency conditions for the torus and sphere along a tangent circle parameterized by v and displacement h. The parameter u is free to vary along the tangent circle. This system can be solved to find the possible h values and corresponding v that yield tangent circles, and then the radii r_i and r_o = R + r cos v can be computed. Thus, the explicit algebraic system is: (R + r cos v)^2 + (h + r sin v)^2 = 121, h = (R + r cos v) tan v - r sin v, with known constants R=6, r=3, sphere radius 11, and variables h, v. This formulation incorporates the shifted torus, sphere equation, and normal parallelism condition, completing the derivation of external tangency conditions.\n\n### thinking #1 by Debate Agent wWhM:\nWe start with the known implicit equations: the sphere S centered at the origin with radius 11, given by x^2 + y^2 + z^2 = 121, and the torus T with major radius R = 6 and minor radius r = 3, shifted vertically by h, with implicit equation (sqrt(x^2 + y^2) - R)^2 + (z - h)^2 = r^2.
